Every time you call a tool, you will receive a dictionary containing the outputs. For example, if you call `get_velocity` on `object_1`, the return might be:
{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

You only have **one chance** to answer the question. When you're confident, submit your final answer using:
`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



Since this problem is a comparison problem, your answer should be the object id number (as a plain number, e.g. `2`, NOT `object_2`) of the object that satisfies the task.
If all objects being compared to each other satisfy the task, output `0`. 
If some satisfy the task, while other objects do not, output the object id numbers of the objects that satisfy the task, separated by commas.

***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

Every time you call a tool, you will receive a dictionary containing the outputs. For example, if you call `get_velocity` on `object_1`, the return might be:
{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

You only have **one chance** to answer the question. When you're confident, submit your final answer using:
`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



Since this problem is a comparison problem, your answer should be the object id number (as a plain number, e.g. `2`, NOT `object_2`) of the object that satisfies the task.
If all objects being compared to each other satisfy the task, output `0`. 
If some satisfy the task, while other objects do not, output the object id numbers of the objects that satisfy the task, separated by commas.

***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



Since the problem is a computation problem, your answer should be ONLY the calculated number that satisfies the task,
rounded to the nearest thousandths place if applicable.
Do NOT include units (e.g. output `3.27` not `3.27 m/s`).
If the task asks for multiple values, separate them with commas (e.g. `20.2, 69.4`).

***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Every time you call a tool, you will receive a dictionary containing the outputs. For example, if you call `get_velocity` on `object_1`, the return might be:
{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

You only have **one chance** to answer the question. When you're confident, submit your final answer using:
`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



Since this problem is a comparison problem, your answer should be the object id number (as a plain number, e.g. `2`, NOT `object_2`) of the object that satisfies the task.
If all objects being compared to each other satisfy the task, output `0`. 
If some satisfy the task, while other objects do not, output the object id numbers of the objects that satisfy the task, separated by commas.

***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

Every time you call a tool, you will receive a dictionary containing the outputs. For example, if you call `get_velocity` on `object_1`, the return might be:
{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

Every time you call a tool, you will receive a dictionary containing the outputs. For example, if you call `get_velocity` on `object_1`, the return might be:
{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

You only have **one chance** to answer the question. When you're confident, submit your final answer using:
`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



Since this problem is a comparison problem, your answer should be the object id number (as a plain number, e.g. `2`, NOT `object_2`) of the object that satisfies the task.
If all objects being compared to each other satisfy the task, output `0`. 
If some satisfy the task, while other objects do not, output the object id numbers of the objects that satisfy the task, separated by commas.

***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

Every time you call a tool, you will receive a dictionary containing the outputs. For example, if you call `get_velocity` on `object_1`, the return might be:
{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

You only have **one chance** to answer the question. When you're confident, submit your final answer using:
`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



Since this problem is a comparison problem, your answer should be the object id number (as a plain number, e.g. `2`, NOT `object_2`) of the object that satisfies the task.
If all objects being compared to each other satisfy the task, output `0`. 
If some satisfy the task, while other objects do not, output the object id numbers of the objects that satisfy the task, separated by commas.

***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



Since this problem is a comparison problem, your answer should be the object id number (as a plain number, e.g. `2`, NOT `object_2`) of the object that satisfies the task.
If all objects being compared to each other satisfy the task, output `0`. 
If some satisfy the task, while other objects do not, output the object id numbers of the objects that satisfy the task, separated by commas.

***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

Every time you call a tool, you will receive a dictionary containing the outputs. For example, if you call `get_velocity` on `object_1`, the return might be:
{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

You only have **one chance** to answer the question. When you're confident, submit your final answer using:
`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

rounded to the nearest thousandths place if applicable.

If the task asks for multiple values, separate them with commas (e.g. `20.2, 69.4`).

***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

Every time you call a tool, you will receive a dictionary containing the outputs. For example, if you call `get_velocity` on `object_1`, the return might be:
{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

You only have **one chance** to answer the question. When you're confident, submit your final answer using:
`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



Since this problem is a comparison problem, your answer should be the object id number (as a plain number, e.g. `2`, NOT `object_2`) of the object that satisfies the task.
If all objects being compared to each other satisfy the task, output `0`. 
If some satisfy the task, while other objects do not, output the object id numbers of the objects that satisfy the task, separated by commas.

***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



Since the problem is a computation problem, your answer should be ONLY the calculated number that satisfies the task,
rounded to the nearest thousandths place if applicable.
Do NOT include units (e.g. output `3.27` not `3.27 m/s`).
If the task asks for multiple values, separate them with commas (e.g. `20.2, 69.4`).

***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



Since this problem is a comparison problem, your answer should be the object id number (as a plain number, e.g. `2`, NOT `object_2`) of the object that satisfies the task.
If all objects being compared to each other satisfy the task, output `0`. 
If some satisfy the task, while other objects do not, output the object id numbers of the objects that satisfy the task, separated by commas.

***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

Every time you call a tool, you will receive a dictionary containing the outputs. For example, if you call `get_velocity` on `object_1`, the return might be:
{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

You only have **one chance** to answer the question. When you're confident, submit your final answer using:
`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

Every time you call a tool, you will receive a dictionary containing the outputs. For example, if you call `get_velocity` on `object_1`, the return might be:
{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

You only have **one chance** to answer the question. When you're confident, submit your final answer using:
`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

You only have **one chance** to answer the question. When you're confident, submit your final answer using:
`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



Since the problem is a computation problem, your answer should be ONLY the calculated number that satisfies the task,
rounded to the nearest thousandths place if applicable.
Do NOT include units (e.g. output `3.27` not `3.27 m/s`).
If the task asks for multiple values, separate them with commas (e.g. `20.2, 69.4`).

***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



Since the problem is a computation problem, your answer should be ONLY the calculated number that satisfies the task,
rounded to the nearest thousandths place if applicable.
Do NOT include units (e.g. output `3.27` not `3.27 m/s`).
If the task asks for multiple values, separate them with commas (e.g. `20.2, 69.4`).

***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

Every time you call a tool, you will receive a dictionary containing the outputs. For example, if you call `get_velocity` on `object_1`, the return might be:
{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

You only have **one chance** to answer the question. When you're confident, submit your final answer using:
`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



Since the problem is a computation problem, your answer should be ONLY the calculated number that satisfies the task,
rounded to the nearest thousandths place if applicable.
Do NOT include units (e.g. output `3.27` not `3.27 m/s`).
If the task asks for multiple values, separate them with commas (e.g. `20.2, 69.4`).

***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

Every time you call a tool, you will receive a dictionary containing the outputs. For example, if you call `get_velocity` on `object_1`, the return might be:
{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

You only have **one chance** to answer the question. When you're confident, submit your final answer using:
`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

If an attribute has 'n/a' right beside it, that means you CANNOT access that attributes value, so keep that in mind when running through the experiment.

 If there are multiple numbers in the attribute, note that they are in the form of an array to specify the different parameters of the attribute.

Every time you call a tool, you will receive a dictionary containing the outputs. For example, if you call `get_velocity` on `object_1`, the return might be:
{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

You only have **one chance** to answer the question. When you're confident, submit your final answer using:
`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

Every time you call a tool, you will receive a dictionary containing the outputs. For example, if you call `get_velocity` on `object_1`, the return might be:
{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

You only have **one chance** to answer the question. When you're confident, submit your final answer using:
`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



Since this problem is a comparison problem, your answer should be the object id number (as a plain number, e.g. `2`, NOT `object_2`) of the object that satisfies the task.
If all objects being compared to each other satisfy the task, output `0`. 
If some satisfy the task, while other objects do not, output the object id numbers of the objects that satisfy the task, separated by commas.

***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

Every time you call a tool, you will receive a dictionary containing the outputs. For example, if you call `get_velocity` on `object_1`, the return might be:
{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

You only have **one chance** to answer the question. When you're confident, submit your final answer using:
`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



Since the problem is a computation problem, your answer should be ONLY the calculated number that satisfies the task,
rounded to the nearest thousandths place if applicable.
Do NOT include units (e.g. output `3.27` not `3.27 m/s`).
If the task asks for multiple values, separate them with commas (e.g. `20.2, 69.4`).

***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

Every time you call a tool, you will receive a dictionary containing the outputs. For example, if you call `get_velocity` on `object_1`, the return might be:
{"vx": 0.0, "vy": -3.2, "vz": 0.0}

You only have **one chance** to answer the question. When you're confident, submit your final answer using:
`{"tool": "answer", "parameters": {"answer": "<your_answer>"}}`



Since the problem is a computation problem, your answer should be ONLY the calculated number that satisfies the task,
rounded to the nearest thousandths place if applicable.
Do NOT include units (e.g. output `3.27` not `3.27 m/s`).
If the task asks for multiple values, separate them with commas (e.g. `20.2, 69.4`).

***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!

Since the problem is a computation problem, your answer should be ONLY the calculated number that satisfies the task,
rounded to the nearest thousandths place if applicable.
Do NOT include units (e.g. output `3.27` not `3.27 m/s`).
If the task asks for multiple values, separate them with commas (e.g. `20.2, 69.4`).

***FINAL GUIDELINES***

You must call `step` to simulate time progression.

1 simulation step is 0.005 real life seconds, and ALL problems are based off of real life time if seconds are mentioned in the task.

Do not make any assumptions about the positions or states of objects, if you are unsure you can use tools get this information.

The z plane is the vertical plane, and the x and y planes are the horizontal planes.

When answering, use the world coordinate frame with signed values: +x, +y, +z are the positive directions; motion or quantities in the opposite directions must be negative. Report signed vectors and scalars accordingly.

Understand that you can use the tools to gather necessary information pertainig to all objects in the scene, not just the one you are trying to analyze.

If your json format is incorrect - the environment will tell you and the simulator will remain in the same state. If one of your tool calls has incorrect formatting, the previous tool calls will successfully execute but the incorrect tool and subsequent tools will not execute. You will see how your tool call was incorrect and get a chance to retry in the next iteration.

Remember that YOU MUST PROVIDE YOUR REASONING FOR EVERY ACTION you take, and then make sure to add a valid JSON format of an array of tool calls.

***When you are trying to call functions, use a string that goes as object_{object_id} for the object id, and use the name of the function as the tool name.***

 For example, if you were to try and call the function get_velocity on object_1, you would write it as:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}}]
```

 RATHER THAN WRITING IT AS:
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": 1}}]
```

Remember that when giving multiple tool calls, you must give them in ONE SINGLE GO, as shown below.
```json
[{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_1"}},{"tool": "get_velocity", "parameters": {"object_id": "object_2"}}]
```
and so on and so forth.

 As you input multiple tool calls, the simulator will run each of them sequentially, and then return the results of each tool call in the order they were called.

 DO NOT GIVE MORE THAN ONE SET OF TOOL CALLS AT A TIME, OR THE SIMULATOR WILL NOT WORK, AND END UP GIVING YOU AN ERROR FOR JSON SYNTAX!!!
